Plus, something about opening a restaurant here and hardly speaking enough English to get the simplest requests right the first time seems silly. The food doesn't make up for it either.

<Text>Had the Kaiseki Lunch Course ($140). I think they only have this available on Sundays and it is hard to nab a spot so make sure you make a reservation by reaching out to the restaurant! This place is in a inconspicuous spot, but oh my it is a hidden gem!

The courses were all amazing, and I loved them all. They even had Nodoguro!! Delicious. The hostess was so warm and friendly as well. And their red bean basque cheesecake is so unique, never had anything like it. The Kaiseki here is on par with some of the more high end and pricey places in San Francisco, but I love the homey and authentic atmosphere of this place!

One thing I would suggest is for the Kaiseki, to have a menu or course description so I would be able to memorialize everything I was eating (though of course the hostess explained everything in great detail, but personally I am more of a reader).

Will definitely be back!!</Text>< user_id>

<review>When you taste something new and you are so sorry you'd never tasted it before... well this was that experience.. I'm so glad our son took us here before leaving SF. Don't  be fooled by the non-descript appearance of the restaurant, coz the food's delish!<//review><rate>5<//rate><user_name>Jankel Friedman</user_name><user>102873225367143078055<//user></record></dataset><record>
< text>
I had the Tori Paitan ramen and the broth had a lot of chicken flavor. It had a very creamy texture and it would have been easy to drink all of it. It came with the thinner noodles, which for my personal preference is only ok, but the star of the dish was the broth! I think you get different noodles depending on what you order. The other toppings were tasty.
I got to try my mom's vegetarian soy milk based ramen broth and it tasted surprisingly savory. As a meat eater, I wouldn't mind ordering a bowl.
It's great that this shop has options for non-pork and non-meat eating people, especially since the Bay Area is so diverse. The atmosphere is exactly like a small cafe in Japan, complete with harp style Ghibli music. Would come back here again :)<//text>

<Rate>5</Rate><gmap_id>0x808f77b3c1ad5df1:0xc798222cab7a1196<//gmap_id><user>102060784065029072375</user><user_name>Richard Chen (Rich)< /user_name><resp>{'time': 1517636719481, 'text': 'Thank you!'}<//resp><Pictures>None<//Pictures><Text>Fellow Bay Area ramen enthusiasts: It's time to escape the tyranny of tonkotsu broth, and Hachi under new ownership is your getaway vehicle.

Weekday lunch visit as a single diner. The soft-opening state is obvious as I think the owner was single-handedly running the floor. It's a small 20-seat place, but don't expect speedy service just yet. For now I'd advise against going as a big group, or during peak hours.

Ordered and really enjoyed the "Shoyu Ontama Tori-ffle Ramen," Chicken Kara-age, and Kyoto Beer (by Kizakura, the sake brewer!)

The Kara-age was fine, if not outstanding. The beer was novel.

But the ramen broth, everyone, is fan-freaking-tastic: Nice, gentle chicken-based broth, seasoned with soy sauce and a dash of black truffles. This last touch, maybe modeled after TSUTA in Tokyo, adds a fabulous aroma that makes this a nice departure from the usual fare. Thin noodles, good texture. The chicken "chashu" was tender, and the ontama soft egg was perfectly executed.

Broth was lovely to the last drop. Certainly don't leave any of it behind.

All in all a nice bowl that doesn't leave you feeling like you'd just had a cheeseburger, served by thoughtful and sincere people. On my next visit I'd love to try the asari clam ramen, I'm craving for some well-done seafood broth in the Bay Area.

Definitely added to my restaurants-near-SFO rotation!</Text><Time>1577634781384< /Time></record></dataset><record>

<date>1572815266241</date><rate>5< /rate><Review>I am giving Saryo Hachi 5 stars. I really couldn't find any other raman place that I can come back as often as coming here. I know many reviews about their ramen portions are small and the services seems can't cover many people but 5 stars for their ramen quality and many dishes will grow on you that you'll want to be back again and again.

Before you come, you need to know it's a small restaurant with one masterchef aka the owner and you get the ramen from the master chef so it is worth waiting about 15-30mins. In fact there aren't much wait on the weekdays when I come around 6:30-7PM I get seated for two ASAP, and food comes usually within 15 mins. If it's about 30 mins of wait I can tell you the wait is still better than many other ramen restaurants in the Bay Area.

The environment is very cozy, actually perfect for coming with your date or significant others. You'll get to have some conversations then the food comes and enjoy a nice meal together.

Parking is very easy to find. I'm really happy with our commute everytime I come.

Food wise, the owner is from Osaka / Kyoto area so the Ramens are chicken broth base ( harder to find and usially people uses pork broth but more oily) and thinner noodles which is excellent for better digest compare to thicker noodles.

Below are our recommendations if you're here for the first time:

Saryo Salad - absolutely beautiful, healthy and delicious. We love the warm tomatoes that matches perfectly with the fresh salad. They decorated the salad with flowers that you can eat and they are so pretty that I always love enjoy the taste and pleased by the look.

Ton-ffle (sliced pork + truffle ) or Tori-ffle (sliced chicken + truffle) ramen. The soup base are chicken broth and soy sauce. More than the truffle, my highlight of the bowl is actually the poach egg, it's so smooth and matches perfectly to the ramen broth. We don't really ask for lighter or heavy taste on the broth and it's always perfect for us. Sometimes I actually think they gave us more noodles than usual but it doesn't hurt to note the service you want less or more noodles.

We come at least once a week for one year, food is consistent and we love that we don't feel thirsty after we dine at Saryo. We feel healthy.

Btw their bathroom flowers are real and arranged by the owner. Saryo is always pleasant to visit and I appreciate it. We highly recommend to our family, friends and coworkers.</Review>< pictures>

< review>
Ramen Saryo Hachi was the worst ramen I have ever eaten. To be very clear and brutally honest, I am a lover of ramen. I'd like to try every new ramen place in California especially the Bay Area. The broth taste was very dull, the meat was very thin, and the noodle was very tasteless. For the price that's generally $14.00 what we get is not very satisfying. More so the ramens are tasteless! And on top of that, the service was really bad/ugly. First of all, the owner, Yuko was not patience in introducing the menu to me. When I asked, "What's the most popular ramen people order here since I am new customer?" She answered, "I made the ramen, of course they all good!" Then when I asked, "What's the difference between clear broth and white broth ramen?" She answered, "It's the same chicken broth but one I made it clear, the other I made it white!" Finally I ordered the clear ramen on the menu. It took a while before she brought it to my table. And when I asked whether it was wasabi in regards to the spicy sauce on the menu $.50 cent that I ordered with the ramen soup she said "I would not sell wasabi with a cheap price like that!". I have been eating ramen/udon in many places, I never felt so insulted that someone would actually thought about the price instead of explaining what wasabi is to me. I thought it was wasabi because the hot sauce she brought to my table looks like wasabi, it has a green color. And I am allergic to wasabi.  Now that I think of it, I never get charged for any hot sauce that I ordered, but I would not mind to pay for it since I ordered it, but the way she answered, "I would not sell wasabi with a cheap price like that!" made me felt really bad! After that I just ate the ramen that I ordered and gave $50.00 cash to pay for that tasteless ramen!< /review>

<name>L Marchiondo Imaging</name><pics>None</pics>< text>
I was recommended to visit Fleet Feet from a few teammates in my roller derby league. I have flat feet, older quad skates, and skating backwards and/or doing fast feet manuevors was causing me extreme pain in my toes and plantar region of both feet.

I brought my skates in and within one minute of entering, I was greeted offered assistance. The young man who walked me through our innersole choices was patient and knowledgeable. They even let me slip my skates on to try out three different SUPERfeet innersoles which I did NOT except!!

The woman that rang up my order was also kind and welcoming (I am now in their system to rack up those points). This was my first visit to Fleet Feet but it is not my last!< /text>

<text>Not a 4-star experience...

We stayed at the Hotel Shattuck Plaza during our first trip to Berkeley, hoping for a luxurious home base for our first getaway as a couple in three years.  Needless to say, nothing about our experience "wowed" us, and certainly didn't meet the standard for a 4-star hotel.  First, we struggled with our personal safety and that of our rental car, given the homeless population living on both Allston Way and Shattuck Avenue.  Additionally, we upgraded to a Deluxe King room, but felt cramped inside the room with about 2 feet of clearance between the bed and the walls on all sides.  Our first impression upon entering our room was hearing the guests in the room next door using the facilities.  We could literally hear everything through the paper-thin walls, which felt disgusting and bizarre.  Not to mention all of the trash trucks traveling up and down Allston at 6:30 in the morning.  It was like every trash truck in the city was on the same route.  TV was okay - not a smart TV and no app usage.  Around 20 channels offered through cable.  Finally, with the restaurant and bar being closed due to the pandemic, we felt as if we didn't experience any amenities during our stay, save reasonable free wifi.

We've stayed in historic hotels before, and can understand the limitations of room size, but the noise transfer was simply unacceptable.  We asked for restaurant recommendations from the front desk during check-in, and were given one offering with a less than confident recommendation.  I understand that the pandemic has impacted the hotel industry in significant ways, but is the hotel asking themselves how to uphold their 4-star rating in the midst of these changes?< /text><rate>2<//rate></record></dataset><record>

< Text>
The hotel is very central in Berkeley, making access to everything an easy walk. As importantly, we came from SFO to there and it was practically door to door with using BART (train). The room was comfortable, clean and attractive. As we were only there for one night, the fact that we were looking out onto pipes and roof surfaces was no problem. We loved the fact that we could open the windows. Its been many years since I have been in a hotel that did that.Downsides - no fridge, no kettle and with 2 paper cups as the option and a water section of the coffee maker to fill, required a bit of problem solving. I was glad that I had brought my own mug. The water container doesnt make quite a full mug of tea though.< /Text>

< text>
My sister's luggage got stolen. Out of the storage room at the front desk. Caught on camera.

3 weeks prior to our wedding, and my wife calls to book some tables at the restaurant downstairs for the morning after the wedding. She comes to find out, by her own initiative, that the restaurant is closing the week of our wedding block. No one called to tell us. We now had nowhere for our guests to mingle, get to know each other, which was a big deal to us. We started to call management, which was a mission to get anyone to call us back. It was a week before we finally got a high level person to communicate back with us, which is now two weeks till our wedding. Their solution was they would offer a European breakfast in a meeting room daily. But there would be no bar, and the breakfast was only open for certain times, as well as no lunch or dinner.

We were quite frustrated/upset since they DID NOT inform us, we found out on our own, and wondered and asked why they chose our weekend to start. Through conversation, they let it slip that they also had now moved my wife to a new room to get ready in, not the bridal suite that we had booked months prior. They decided to change the carpets in that hallway to the suite. No one called prior to inform/ask/come up with a solution, again it was on our call to address the restaurant situation. My wife planned 95% of our wedding, every detail. This was huge, as she had 10 people getting ready in her room. I think every bride can relate that to swap out the bridal suite to something different and smaller is a huge wrench to throw at someone. They would not release us from our room contract, even though they were not delivering what was agreed to. They gave my wife a smaller suite, which they comped.

The weekend rolls around, and we start checking in. We leave welcome bags at the front desk, some of which were not passed out to our guests. Guests would check in without linens and towels in their room, their room wasn't ready by 4pm. The A/C didn't work in some of the rooms, forcing guests to change rooms. My uncle is pretty sure he got bit by bed bugs, as his feet were covered in bites. The European breakfast they provided in the meeting room, their solution which was just deli meats and croissants, ran out of food by 8:30am. Which doesn't do much when most places don't open to eat till 10, 11am in the area. The fire alarm goes off Saturday morning at 8am, which was a false alarm because of the construction crew. The hotel would comp Friday night, but only if you asked for it.

But what topped it off, as I'm landing back home late Sunday night from my amazing wedding, was turning my phone on to a text from my sister that said her luggage had been stolen, all of it. The luggage she had checked in the front desk to store for a few hours. Mine and my wife's luggage had been stored at the same time, with all our wedding gifts in them. And only hers had been stolen. It seemed too coincidental and lucky for us that the bags stolen were right next to ours.

Their response to everything has been insulting. From our first contact with Ashley and Carol regarding the room/restaurant situation, to Greg, the GM being involved, has been opposite of hospitality. We constantly had to seek their feedback out, continuously got nowhere, and the solutions they presented along the way were laughable. They call themselves a 4-star hotel, but have management and employees that are not worthy of a 1-star Motel 6. We had to fight to have our rooms comped that we did. Our guests paying $240 a night had no working AC and getting woken up by false fire alarms on the weekend? And when it came to my sister's luggage being stolen, out of their storage room, by a random person, caught on video, he deflected it to insurance and had no follow up. My sister and myself had to chase him down to find out the status of things. Which as of today, has STILL NOT BEEN PAID OUT TO HER.

We also have made the decision to not stay at any BPR Properties hotels based on what they have let happen to this hotel.< /text>

<time>1387129152859</time><rating>3< /rating><review>Renovated with a modern feel. It's convenient to downtown, with nearby bars, restaurants, and public transit options. There's no free parking, but a self-park deck ($) is across the street. Free WiFi, coffee maker (Keurig with K-cups), friendly service, you know, the usual for a high-end hotel (you're paying for it, after all).

As for the downsides, the room was a bit cramped (we had 3 in a room), there was no dresser, and closet space was minimal, though oddly, the bathroom was still large. Speaking of the bathroom, ours didn't really have a door, just a loose barn-style sliding door panel with frosted glass. No thanks. Given the room arrangement, a pocket door would've been a much better choice. Also, our room faced the main street, which made it a bit noisy at night.

Be aware that electricity to the rooms is only activated once you insert your room key - don't expect your devices to charge when you are gone.<//review><pictures>None</pictures>< user>

< review>
The hotel is very nice located right in the heart of Berkeley by UC Berkeley. There is a target nearby as well as many different restaurants with different kinds of food such as thai, american, japanese, bhurmese, indian, even chipotle, etc. The rooms are very nice and clean. Beds are confortable, sheets are clean. There is a restaurant downstairs at the lobby. There is no parking provided. There is a parking garage across you can pay for, there is metered parking right in front if yoy are lucky enough to get a parking. The metered parking is only metered between 9am-6pm, so overnight parking is fine. Hotel employees were very friendly, helpful, and patient.</review>

This is an out of ordinary kind act-----the other day when the power is off in downtown Berkeley, the place that I need to make copies---Fed Ex is closed early due to teh power outrage, I turned to the closest location with lighting---Hotel Shattuck, hoping they may be able to help me to make a few copies, but not with high hope. I asked the front desk gentleman who was not sure if their machine is working, so he checked with another gentleman , who, quickly and generously said yes, and spent around 20-25 minutes to make copies for me, I offered to pay, but he declined politely.   Without his help---which he is not obligated to, because I am not their guest, I would not be able to send my mail on time the next day to meet the deadline. At my request, he told me his name is Adam McFarlin., dir. of room service.
This positive experience proves once again that kind people are everywhere, and that Hotel Shattuck 's  nice customer service has extended to people who are even not their customers.!!!< /text>

< time>
1383006061479< /time>
<Rating>4</Rating>< text>
Located right downtown, this historic (but renovated) mission-style hotel was actually the first in Berkely (opened in 1910). It has a nice restaurant inside, but is walking distance to lots of places nearby for easy exploring. Despite the corporate ownership, I always like staying in a boutique hotel over a major chain. They have your standard amenities like a gym, a bar, a restaurant, and free WiFi. Self-parking is next door, but they are really close to public transportation via BART which is what I recommend if you plan on visiting San Francisco.</text>
